dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to persistent catarrh and common colds, and you see small eyes and eyelashes, and weakening of vision, and burned paper; and the man's hair turns gray, and his head is full of ague pain, and the patient sneezes. When the eyelids open completely and nothing comes from disturbing the heart or diminution, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal him, then apply suction cups or a hat without piercing in order to draw out impurities, then place on the eye (the mixture made of myrrh and aloe and incense and sarcorrhaphia), and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths; and the method for the cloths should be that you take cloths that are sufficiently soft and double each one in half, and then place them one on top of another according to the amount that the eyelids need; then strain from above with a hard cloth formed into strips, and repeat the suction cups without piercing; then remove the suction cups and let the eye strain day and night, and if the bandages loosen, it is necessary that you strain as much; then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it's good; if not, continue with plastering and cloths and the bandage and suction cups until it heals.

de la bowe de l’oil	From the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" only comes from water that accumulates in the ear, resembling descending fluid, and it's not real fluid; and how this condition appears is by having the patient sit upright with their head straight, then grab the back of the head with both hands and move it until you see the fluid come up to your nostrils; then remove it, don't let it fall again and clear out any light, and see what the patient sees; and if it doesn't come down suddenly, know that it's real fluid, and if the movement from the water isn't as described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. des aigues de l’oil	Of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the indications for performing incisions, and what needs to be pierced; we perform this according to health.

It is necessary that you make the patient lie between your hands in the shade away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand where its eyes are close together, or on your right hand where they are apart. Then take with your right hand (if they're close together), insert an instrument called 'almagda' onto the paper held by your left hand, or vice versa. Place the tip of the tool beneath the crown through a width of about one finger across the corneal surface to the area slightly below the inner corner of the eye, then push the 'almagda' tool in a forceful manner and rotate your hand until it punctures into the corneal surface, feeling that 'almagda' has reached the empty part. The measure of the path of 'almagda' should match the size of the space from the pupil to the edge of darkness; this is the crown of the eye. If you see bone through the transparency of the cornea in this paper, then place your tool until it reaches where water is or the exit point, then expel debris bit by bit afterwards.

de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the nose

None of the times give birth to or produce various tied creatures, from which some seem like scorpions with the foot of a hen; and if there are such things or if there is a worm with an orange color, and if it has fat with good color.

de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the nose

quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and stitched.

de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums

des sordens	Of cautery by fire, command to the diseased person to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their origin, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

Many times they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and ugly and hard scabs; and it happens many times that a black tooth and citrine and worms exist until corruption reaches the gum, and then the tooth becomes stinky. Many times the pain will lead you to cough, and be aware of whether it is tooth pain or not. And when you are certain about which tooth hurts, it's necessary that you sear around the tooth with a heated instrument for at least one or two seconds so as to prevent gum irritation everywhere. And if the tooth is pierced and fractured, it is necessary for you to fill it with cloths, where the fracture occurred; and if you gently squeeze it between the tongs while pulling, without breaking it during the pull; and it must be very carefully opened under the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure to guard that you do not break it and leave a part, and warn the patient of greater pain from the root's malice than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And remember not to do as the ignorant doctors do, who break the tooth once due to their haste and boldness, without applying what we have mentioned; but let this disease take its course through the roots where they remain or through the tooth itself that they break, just like we often suggest. And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or vinegar and water; and if bleeding occurs, which happens quite often, apply vinegar to the wound; and if it doesn't work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, by which you make your teeth first, should be with long points and large handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend upon pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays during bleeding, it is necessary that you place wet cotton with butter on the wound for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the legs are bent, and you hold the tongs that are called "algefri", making it seem like a well-tended mouth; they should also be done in such a way as a file would be, this is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge through all these clamps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh up to the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is known as palmache, as follows:

Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if assistance is taken with this tool which has two spouts, as shown below:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the order of teeth, and this tool which seems like large pliers, as depicted below:

For there are parts of diseases where the old did not teach any instrument because of the diversity in some and if they break from the carriage or from other bones, or if it decays, then when he searches for the tools that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, which is shown here, this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well holding so as to hold the bone without it escaping, but able to hold and remove it; and then restore in its place the medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then seek all that instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and the shape is ugly, even in virgin women if it's necessary that you know whether the teeth are grown after the tooth, and they are not in their rightful position, and one cannot pull or file them: then remove them; and if they adhere with the tooth, take this instrument as depicted here, and resembles two small beaks, and should be made of sharp iron at its tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge is thin and thin in my hands by the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, so I file with a single file as it is shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used for making needles; and in filing I make the tooth thin and thin in my hands gently, so that you do not move it until it finishes cutting; then smooth out at the end with any smoother, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it's necessary to file down the roughness until it becomes flat, so that it doesn't hurt the tongue or damage speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is before the gum, or through percussion or impact, and when the patient cannot press upon what they eat that it doesn't cause bleeding, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, if this does not work; then you should restrict them with a thread of gold, as silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And use threads neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth spreading outwards, take the thread and bend it in half between the healthy teeth, then place the dislocated teeth between the toothless spaces, if there is one or more, until you can feel the healthy tooth on the other side. Then restart the covering process up to the area where you had covered before, and move your hand skillfully and carefully, not allowing it to move at all; and bind your tie tightly around the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then bind the teeth with thread using tweezers, and join them together, then place them between a healthy tooth and the tongue, and position it so as not to irritate the tongue; and then let it stay in this tightness as much as possible, if they dislocate or the threads come off, you should replace with another thread; if it stays in this condition and serves for all its duration, and this is how the teeth are shaped and how the position of the two healthy back teeth and the two front ones works, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth gets dislodged, if you return it to its place, step by step, just as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't suitable or can withstand it, and never make a shape of an ox bone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and tighten it as we have said, and stays and serves this long duration.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the threads come from under the tongue or are natural as we are born with them; or by accident in sewn wounds; and the procedures should be performed when you work on the mouth for the patient, have your head above a healthy tooth, and lift the tongue; then cut out the nerve thread as wide as possible until the tongue is removed from its position, and if there's stiffness or swelling, it's due to a wound healing quickly, so bend the hook and cut the thread; and remember not to make the incision too deep because there is an artery underneath; and once you're done, lift the upper part back to pinkish color and cool water, then put a linen tent under the tongue; and wash your hands each night, ensuring the teeth cannot adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put sulfur on the wound; and if it doesn't stop, apply gentle cauterization using a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat with other remedies until the patient recovers.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it's of rust color or black or hard, but your patient doesn't feel pain, do not touch it as it is an ulcer; and if it begins to turn yellow and there's moisture, then pinch the hook and drain with a subtle spasm, and release from both sides; and if your tongue fails to come back in your treatment, apply vinegar until it dries out, then return to your work until you have used all force; then lift the head from cool water and salty water, and cure him with other remedies until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	None of the nodes in the throat that are called 'godath' come inside, and they're properly referred to as the second pair. When you treat them, as we've mentioned earlier during division, if they don't heal, then take care: If these are hard swellings with small sensitivity and a reddish color, then do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron for bleeding purposes; but let them heal until they fester. Then you may remove them, or they might burst on their own. If they have a whitish color and the root is slender, prepare your instrument to cover them, but first check if the swelling has calmed down and healed completely.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and place his limbs on your healthy side, and have him open his mouth and the attendant press his tongue completely onto all the instrument, as this is how it's done; and use silver or finely crafted iron tools just like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue to all this tool, and you see the pus-filled lump, take the tincture and put it into the almond, then pull it up more than you can; and don't remove anything from the layers with it, then push against the tool in a way that resembles pressing something strong; and the head is tied together, one part after another, and they're very sharp, made of silver or copper:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool available now, just use tweezers, like this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make cuts on one side and the other; and when you have made a cut in one of the cheeks, then make the same cut on the other according to this same manner, and after the incision gargle with the hot sick patient's saliva, or gargle with both hot and mild water, and when bleeding occurs, then gargle again with hot water, or use cooked green grape pits, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until all of the pus is cleared; then proceed with the treatment until it has healed; and no new abscesses form in the throat other than the two cheeks, so treat them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, to be specific the small abscess; and had well sealed off the entire throat so much that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage way, and she could neither eat nor drink, thus dying if she continued like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had caused two streams of pus to be released through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I immediately proceeded quickly, inserting one into the first lymph node, then pulling it out, and removing a large portion of pus. Then I made another incision in the other area near the nose, and I had his mouth open and pressed his tongue; afterwards, I inserted the needle into this abscess, and took out some of it, only leaving a little blood to escape; and thus he was drained of his throat channel, and began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting from this wound for a long time; and the abscesses were growing again immediately, filling the place I had emptied, until it became quite large; then I closed him up and cauterized inside his throat: thus he remained without growing. And I left those parts, only God made of him after me.
de l’uve	Regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it descends into the uterus, and it swells and becomes long, this is called "perpendicular"; and if it is offside large and round, this is called "ovum".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure doesn't help, and you see that the abscess has calmed down and is subtle, then it's necessary to handle it; and if it's round when assembled and not long, and it's blood-red or reddish-brown or black, then it's necessary to avoid making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.

Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said before regarding its blueness and length, you should have the patient stand in front of the sun and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned previously. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut too much, you injure the voice and speech. And after incision, use what we have instructed regarding incisions to the two amandros (i.e., ducts), and treat until the wound heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if their organs give off a fowl smell due to cutting, it is necessary that you apply the means of cautery for the sense organ.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of cautery is like hot iron.

Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair or where we put the medicine, like movements of a spoon, and place the tool with all the medicine on top of the ovule; and make sure the disease stays within its own limit, so that saliva and mucus flow from its mouth into the medicine inside, not descending to the throat or causing inflammation; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the ovule for half an hour's worth of quantity, until you see it absorbed and the reactions to the medicine are calmed down; and if you see this happening, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool on top of the cotton in the wick above, until the cotton is heated by the ovule; and repeat this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and cleanse after four or five days. And if you need to start the medicine cautery again, do so, and after the cautery, clean around the ovule with cotton soaked in butter; and rinse from cold water, and gargle until it's healed completely.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or using the cautery; if it's treated with steam according to this method, take calamus, myrrh, and thyme along with rue and chamomile and parsley and similar herbs, and combine all of them or any of these in one pot, put them inside and let it boil; make sure the pot is filled tightly with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place a hairpin according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be of silver or lead, and whether one of the shoulder joints is placed in the mouth against the wound until the vapor ascends to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes inflamed; after that you repeat often, until the eye dries out, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of pus discharge, for many things occur; and do not perform this action as the pus starts to drain.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a stick and place an eggshell in the chief's mouth, so that the wound does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to affect the mouth, and it is a good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times one finds in the throat bone or spinal part of a fish without anything; therefore, it is necessary that you remove what you can see and press your tongue to the sun with all the instrument until you see movement; and whatever does not open up and remains in the throat, it is appropriate for you to induce vomiting so that the malady leaves as if the meat was cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing escapes through vomiting; or if the malady swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a small chunk of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when she comes up to your mouth, if she breathes out, and then pull forcefully; and if this does not come out as what we have said, take one tool of thorn according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the forceps be applied to the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head elevated high above; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest anything go wrong, nor push any bone inside; and move when the patient pushes the instrument back out, because if it's moved or the thing is slippery; if it pulls down, or if it drags with equal force on all parts of the instrument until it can drag fully.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the lumen of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the bile treated with medicine alone, as I have said in the division, through medical treatment; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, then you squeeze the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, guide it out entirely with small fractions, or with delicate pincers suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, take a thread-covered rod and guide it into the patient's throat, then force out any blood that has collected in the thread until you hear the thread snap, and perform this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you bathe the patient with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full jug of cold water and pour it into the patient's mouth, then guide it until they swallow it, and move their hands often; and as soon as the blood senses the water, they will defecate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if they do not defecate as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; perform this several times, because it will pass without obstruction.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of fumigation is like this: you take a pot where there are charcoal fires and place it covered with a perforated shield in the middle, and inside that, so close to the fire, are placed the parts of the instrument. Then pour your fumigation into this. Have the patient put the tip of the stick into their mouth, and seal their mouth shut so no smoke can escape but goes right up to their nostrils; then blood will now flow out through them if it doesn't already; and if it doesn't come out, start the fumigation repeatedly several times. And let the patient be thirsty and eat salty things, etc., don't drink water; and then they must leave this way out with this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to clear mucus is such that when it can be seen, it resembles hooked tweezers for pulling out in the throat; and has a resemblance at the tip as if for trimming, and it has roughness like sandpaper, so what she takes cannot be left behind. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are various kinds of abscess discharges, according to what memory suggests from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways about this where one is in its own appearance, and concerning which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those limbs which are inside the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those on the foundation, and the abscesses in the inner thigh differ from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And with abscesses one should not pierce them until the body has completed its development; and for those that must be pierced when they are fully formed and do not complete their development, such as abscesses located near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it remains until it is rotten internally, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, this causes a contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is located within the main limb, and you delay the puncturing until it's completely dead, it will harm the main limb. If it's located at the root, if you pierce or do so even when it's dead; it should not that you perforate a crustous abscess without digestion completed, except for those which are situated at the root and might spread downward, inside, causing fistula; and it cannot heal properly in large quantities.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you know the time of abscess perforation which occurs according to maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and departure of fever, and diminution of pain and heat, and from movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; it should be that the perforation stays above or at the level of the abscess, where it opens outwards. And make the perforation long across the body, and if the abscess is near hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When these fold, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the raw meat, it's better to let the puncturing continue until digestion is fully completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you pierce it before that, it allows the poison of him to spread through his body and fills with many kinds of dirt; and by chance harden the skin and its underlying parts.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no ulcers pierced through the width of the backbone, according to what the body needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you introduce small ulcers, small cuts; and in large ulcers, large cuts, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the ulcer; and if such ulcers require the use of a knife, and covering; when they have become as hard as wooden planks, and are softening, then it is necessary to do it like what's done on babies: and if there are those that split into three angles, and if there are those that are covered similarly to the leaves of bay trees, such as ulcers from angles; and if there are those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and shapes are covered.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those without a head, such as superficial ulcers, it must be that you pierce them completely through. And when the ulcer is large and has gathered much pus, it needs to be punctured, but do not drain all the pus at once in this moment, but drain only part of it; then boil the ulcer until the other side heals, then leave no substance inside; perform this process gradually from larger to smaller sizes, until the pus drains completely. Similarly, if the body is weak or pregnant women, or small children, or elderly and decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For whenever it experiences shaking once with the exit of the bowe, that perhaps kills the patient, and you don't realize this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious in this chapter. When you have incised your abscess, if there is a wound, look to see if the incision from the abscess is small; and if it's a simple cut, you may use linen or old cotton cloths; and if it's large with much pus, then it would be necessary for you to place a wad in each one so that they press against each other. And if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and sewed it together internally, then you should fill it with old cotton or shredded linen without moisture, and bind it up to the third day; then set it, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your operation, cool it down with cold and ease, and apply moisture until you cover the site repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then manage and treat it properly, and use the powders I've mentioned in this book. If it's ice-related, or where your hand or an abscess is very inflamed, you should place wet cloths and blankets in wine and hot oil repeatedly; if it's in a swollen state, and your hand or that lesion is flesh-heavy, you should cover with wet cloths in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for three days as we have said; then remove the pus and clean it, following how it should be done until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know completely in the treatments of abscesses: or I have told you how one should act before treatments of abscesses, and here comes this chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Little ulcers come from the nose, and they are of us that appear in bandages, like a necklace on a cat's head, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and others with moisture just like peas; and there are some that are hard and stony to the knife, and there is no doubt that they contain blood and do not act otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of cutting so is that you must try with every tool called "the introducer", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, you perform it from above for its full length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture has drained out, you scorch so that nothing is left of the skin containing that moisture; for it returns if one leaves nothing behind. Then dip a cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until another day; and this heals what remains from night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And repeat the cotton as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know that it does not linger through the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for the task, while it remains healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the gut not fat, cut it according to this shape, long; and squeeze out its fats, and scrape it from all sides, and apply your entire treatment force onto the cloth where it is; and if the blood flows against you, do as I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly handle the abscess if it is due to a stone, and cut and treat with what I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when it comes to cutting on the stone-abscess and the wetness, it is more delicate, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or head or there is no moisture, and of these newly-formed abscesses that I observed or the head of an elderly woman; and found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and even if one had pierced none, it would have been just as well to make incisions on it as on a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or around the head, it was that those which come from children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be for as long days as possible depending on the individual, so that the pus may emerge; and treat them according to how they should be treated.
des scrophules	of the scrophula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times such abscesses occur in the throat, and around the necks, and during attacks, and not once come elsewhere or on any part of the body, they are small, and they intertwine with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly inside its coat, like the ear and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scabs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those where you see a good condition in the throat, and it resembles the color of blood, silent on each side and not penetrating under the neck or near the artery or ducts, and not deeply; you should take care to handle it from above, and shave off each part, and make cuts along both lips of the heart if necessary, as we have described in abscesses on the head; and do it slowly, making sure you don't cut the nerve or blood vessel, nor let out too much fluid, that your hands do not escape, and do not go too far ahead, so as not to remove more than what is required.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it doesn't allow you to open [it], put in the wound vitriol broil, or any powders that stop blood flow, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and starts to decompose.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood has been absorbed [after bleeding], return to your work until it is completed; then according to your skill's measure, if there are any small nodules remaining, remove and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the nodule, it should not be that you remove that nodule from its root but rather bind it with a double thread tightly and let it fall out through that part without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then continue treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cure the entire boil, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, then there should be no excess left due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	And it is necessary that you treat its root, and drain it, and stitch it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those boils that contain excess fluid, pierce wherever it opens up; and pierce in such a way as was mentioned before, while depending, then administer ointment and similar things to it, so that the corruption destroys what is left of its decay; and when the wound has been well cleaned, apply ointment until it is solid, as long as it remains healthy.
de squinance	"De squinance" refers to medical practices concerning deformities or abnormalities related to angles or positioning. It could be associated with conditions affecting bones, joints, muscles, or other bodily structures where the natural alignment is disrupted. This term might cover a variety of scenarios from anatomical malformations due to birth defects, injuries sustained over time, or diseases that alter body parts' normal orientation and function. In medieval contexts, such knowledge would have been part of the extensive medical and surgical practices aimed at diagnosing, treating, and sometimes correcting these abnormalities.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and wrote about neck surgery; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is the inscription of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not help this, because all the veins and lungs are near in the body for those who have abscesses deep within their mouth, or in their throat or between two bones.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the bronchial channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut across three circles or four small slits through, between two of them. By the amount of the slit in this way, not in the cartilage; and let this be sufficient for sectioning the epiglottis so that there is no meat, and the vessels are long enough to prevent it from being too short.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all oncine, then cut through the keur until it reaches the cheneil; and avoid any blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut down the syfac, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the stream from the cheneil which jumps out through the one who is broken, and due to lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, gather the two mouths of the wound as cleanly as possible, and all along the line without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim insists that one should not perform such operations until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient's organs are deemed dead, and the deficiency has been achieved.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut on the epiglottis because the organs can't evacuate, and he breathes through the wound, and so he is protected from death; and to command the old men to leave the wound open until the malady's illness has passed, and it has passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and clean it, as long as it was treated; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife and stabbed it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe. And I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found where the blood was issuing from it, and indeed she had no cut veins or conduits other than her throat, and the wind went in through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I quickly tended to the wound and treated her until she was healed; and only left her voice hoarse for so long as she lived, and then returned to her usual state afterwards. This is why I say that when cutting the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "glossopharyngeal hernia," and they are large abscesses in the color of a raisin, and occur mostly in women. They can occur in two ways: naturally or by accident; natural ones do not involve any effort.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidents occur in two ways. One resembles fat from us, and the other way resembles an abscess coming from our artery; there is fear involved, and it's not advisable to apply a cauterizing substance elsewhere but only on small ones, with proof and careful inspection of every intervention: if you find it just like fat we have, and cannot reach any vein, cut it out similarly to how we cut fat, and remove all its covering tissue; if there is none; search well and treat it accordingly until it's completely healed.
des nous	From our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways exist for us, so I will mention all similarities; and it is fitting that I explain the entire distinction between us and its outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that in the state of fever and illness, it lasts as long as the boiling (of bodily processes) has not passed, and is accompanied by putrefaction; thus, once the fever and heat have subsided.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	In the case of the healthy one, there is no fever, no pain and it contains lymph, which is its own sac and is along the body's color, starts also like a boil, and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, oily or moist, and most of the colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treating the new, you should first inspect and inquire about all the instrument which is called 'entromissory', according to its shape or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of incising abscesses in us is that you take or more moist than what you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers a little at a time, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the pus, and be careful not to rupture.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the wound is moist, whatever its color might be, if you cut it as I said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come out, know that it is fatty, then cut it crosswise, take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape it from all sides and keep the bandage where it lies. And if you cannot remove the wound clean, then pull it in pieces so nothing remains stuck inside.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is nothing stuck inside, the wound will repeatedly return over many times; and if it sticks a bit but doesn't bother you, fill the wound with some corrosive powders and water, hold the wound in place, and apply soothing substances to treat abscesses hotly, and continue other treatments until it becomes clean; and if the wound is large, then cover the edges of the wound with two layers of material, and treat the infection that causes discharges.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too small or another issue arises causing urgency, use the left over vitriol from the process and let it sit for two days or three, as long as the wound is healing, then rest the body with blood baths; then return to the treatment that has been paused due to a new situation.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Look at these instruments for internal discharge and there are three kinds: large, medium-sized, and small. There are four of them known as 'albaret' and one called 'breb'. These have also three types: large, medium, and small to fit the pus-filled fistulas. They're similar to needles used for threading which are yellow in color and made better with black wax when fitting into the curves of a fistula. There are again three kinds: large, medium-sized, and small according to the width of the holes involved.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the clamps are as follows: large, medium-sized, and small. They come in two varieties with three types each based on the number of bends; there are also those that have three bends which come in three kinds too; there are also clamps with two bends, and some just one bend, all these too come in three variations. All of them are necessary according to their size.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this is made to be cut off and for those who do not cut through with force but from one side only, they burn the skin because in such cases one does not cut the vein or nerve; and these penetrating tools are then held in the hands so that the patient does not feel any pain at the opening of abscesses; and there are three ways: large, small, and medium, just as you see; and none of these use force except when cutting fat areas, like legs, arms, nipples, ankles, and alike; and every time another small tool is used, resembling the shears of a barber, according to this shape, on which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And let it remain one time in its healthy position where all veins are properly connected and the arteries too, never once conforming to this grand form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the times do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like breasts of women; and they remain swollen and inflated, and whoever wishes to treat them should follow this form from this line .b. up to .g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Trim the fat, then treat the wound with healing medicine. Then align the two wound edges for stitching and continue treatment until it is healed. If the nipple slants downwards due to its size as in women, cut it into two parts above, by two similar incisions; so one stitch attaches to another at the end of each, ensuring the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then trim the skin between the two edges, remove fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and that which is necessary in treatment until it's healed. If not healed or if the incision isn't fully completed due to the difficulty of healing for the patients or blood leakage, it's necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton wadding in corrosive ointment; leave it until the drainage stops and fat can be removed, then treat until it is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	remove abscesses from the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from the axillae are methods of hard scrofula or when there are nodules, and if they contain moisture.
