de la routure de l’artere	regarding the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is being opened and the skin above it is sewn together, many times pus collections occur, and this also happens with veins and abscesses; and if one knows how to do this properly when it's an artery situation, then the pus collections are long extending downwards. And when you feel resistance with your fingers, that indicates it needs to be grasped firmly; and when it's about a vein opening, it appears with a red appearance above the abscess; and it is foolishness to cut these pus collections, and especially in situations of lacerations and wounds on other parts like neck and body, where they are numerous, and are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It follows that one must avoid iron surgery. For the head it must be avoided as well. And in those cases where the artery is inflamed, do work over the skin along its entire length; then proceed with the incision on the vein, and properly remove the artery from the tissues until it's completely exposed; after this, place a needle underneath and pierce through to the other side, then tie up the artery with double thread in two places as I taught you when extracting two arteries from temples. Then pull out the tissue that is between these two lines with an introducer tool till all the pus comes out, and release the pus collection; after this apply the necessary wound care until it heals over. If the pus collection is due to a vein issue, then coat your hand holding the pus area with the pus throughout the entire skin, place a needle underneath the tissue that you are holding in your hand, pierce through, and use double thread, pulling from the other side; tie up the pus area as I taught previously, or by joining one part of two parts of thread to each shoulder. If you doubt if the threads will pass properly, then insert another needle throughout all layers of the pus with the first needle's thread, and tie off all four ends tightly; after this cut away any excess pus, leaving what is bound; then place a moist cloth with wine and oil on top and apply dressing and ointments until it fully heals.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So, just like abscesses occur in arteries and veins, abscesses of nerves happen when nerves are cut, or due to too much labor, and similar conditions.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	This happens more often with shoulders and elbows as well as in all places where joints are present, this is the issue of abscesses, and its color resembles the color of flesh, appearing in many positions without pain; and when it's restrained firmly, one feels pain inside the patient, not within the flesh but below the skin; and moves entirely from every direction, neither forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and someone with joints doesn't suit covering with metal: an accident could cause constriction; and that which is on head or forehead makes the skin go slack.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez. des grosses boces pendans	Of large warts hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor. Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess inside, and I will come to the treatment of the sore afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bladder burns.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue. Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a simple matter, and opens up well when you press it with your hand, not restraining at all; and if it's due to blood, it opens by these signs - the abscesses are large and hard, and located according to their size; and if it's due to windiness, it sounds hollow in the ear, and you inspect as its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or veins, or windiness.

Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Surgical incisions are openings of veins which require no special technique. And when the surgical incisions age they become thrombosed; and we have discussed similar examples in division and their symptoms, and I will mention here those that respond to treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thromboses, when they occur in the anus, do not show up by touch alone, except for the treatment with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the anus can be felt, and those that can be treated are these.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must put the woman in a cool house, then place her on an altar with tongs, and keep the roots of marjoram covered. Then apply powder made from restaining medicine such as senna, dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar remedies; then soak her feet for an hour, after which she is placed in cold water; if bleeding persists, give her a decoction of sumac, apple peel, and walnut shells among other things. Then take oat flour, mix it with honey and garlic, and use this as plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make her suck on suction cups on the back and nipples without piercing them; then take wool, and the mucus in the juice of plantain or in the juice of agrimony with old wine, and have her suckle at the breast.

de l’enfantement	Regarding childbirth

The profession begins with understanding the natural birth figure and its signs. When you see a woman in labor who is panting heavily, eager to breathe deeply, wanting to smell salt: then knows that the fetus is about to forcefully emerge; thus you learn that this birth occurs naturally according to the natural figure, emerges solely from his head, and follows him immediately; and when you notice these signs, it befittingly press gently on her abdomen, so that the fetus will soon come out; for when he descends through his head, he brings with him the second part, freed of his surplus by proper cleaning. And what comes otherwise does not occur naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier. Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes through its head by natural exit, and the woman is in great pain during childbirth, and her strength is weak, she should sit on a stool, or have women hold her; then let her draw out from where orfenic (possibly meaning 'her own nature') or fenugreek be cooked, and then place the midwife between her hands with a small sparrow, whose form is as follows:

Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed them under a strong magnet, and out came one bone, followed by others after some days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, for it seems that this person's abdomen lacks bones.

I took the wound, and handled its bones as well, until the woman was in her best condition; and I dressed the woman for a long time like this, and it became just a bit swollen around her hand; and I remember this chapter being done only because when the masters find an unusual thing, they need to know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the married one to their place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	After this comes the form of the presser, to which books are attributed; and for two forms each of four limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In every case, the horns should be more delicate than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth should be as wide as half a finger, and the margin of the trees must be so, and long one palm and a half; and in the middle of the two handles there should be two adjustments of this same pipe, which should be tight in both directions, about half a palm from each end or somewhat more; and these two adjustments are fixed inside the mouth of the mortar to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another variant, which seems more subtle and lighter in proportion to its size, can be made from a pipe of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of tongs. Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	All these instruments are arranged at the top and multiplied in their forms; and when you have them set up, your work will be faster, and you'll reach higher positions for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the tool until you have set it up, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est. de percier lou fondement	To pierce the base

de la fistule dou fondement	from the sinus with its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers. If it has passed up to the joint of the ankle, then the plug comes up to the knee; if there is no winding and pain inside, then he will have a hard bow, and it is not worth medicine or immediate treatment by ointment; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure but labor and the vain efforts of foolish people who interfere.

des emorroydes	from bleeding wounds

Disorders occur in two ways: or they are inside the foundation, such as a seed of resin, and if there are small and large ones, and when one or more are inside, and it's beyond the foundation and at its main part; but those which are beyond have little moisture, and still have some drops of citrine water or even a bit of blood, and they have the color of red. dou fremit	The tremble
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A small appearance emerges before the body, and goes all around it; and whenever the veins cool, and one feels this like a death shudder, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a stick made from a goose feather or a strong vulture's feather, and place this stick over the shudder, until the purple circle encompasses the entire shudder; then move your hand to the whole stick while collecting all of it under the shudder, and place it around completely, and spread it outwards, thereby uprooting the shudder from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, do this with an arachnid or iron cane in the form as described, and make it slender everywhere and smooth above and below:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor should it be pierced, for you must hold onto both ends and squeeze. And if you see any trembling, cauterize the tremor, just as it is shown in the section on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	in the form of a bladder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No silver or hot iron, or molten spider or lead should ever be used. And these small and large instruments should not be employed according to who they are intended for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when treating children and those who are weak and painful, use small tools.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the tool being small and large as described above, or how you tie the belly according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there's a need where the belly is bound, just as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and let it be that at one side are two holes, and on the other one. And have the belly with medicines placed in a skin or parchment bag, and pierce all around with small holes. Have each hole approximately one digit apart from its neighbor. Then place one strong, twisted thread through each of these holes, threading them as if to bind a goat; when the medicine is inside, tie it at the front using another thick thread before performing enemas; this creates a circular shape:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and smear the head with oil or chicken yolk or something similar, then gently rub it in. Then instruct your attendants to hold their two hands together while watching him closely until he loses consciousness, then remove the pustule, lift his limbs onto the bed, and if the medicine is seen leaving, pull it out as much as possible; and if he sleeps through a whole night, this will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema in a case of belly discomfort, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as long as he feels well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhage is from their source or from an abscess, or if the pustule is as delicate as for a child; and this is the shape of the delicate pustule on which the skin is restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have discussed the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will discuss treatments for hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on where the wounds are located, and for what reason they were caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The reasons for wounds are due to the injury of bones, the size of a sword and knife cuts, or from spears, clubs, arrows or any similar things; they can also be caused according to what is in the body like wounds on the neck, head, stomach, abdomen, liver, etc., and I will explain how each wound should be treated, beginning with simple head wounds because my memory will come to that part.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound appears or the head is affected, and if no bones are broken, be careful whether it's due to stone or similar issues, and the skin has been completely torn away from the wound, which is large. And you slightly doubt the presence of pus: if there is little blood coming from the wound, then cleanse the scalp immediately, even if a small amount of blood appears, and otherwise, cleanse in opposition to the affected part; and ensure that the body is full of wine and large meats after this procedure.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they do not wish to cleanse with me, reduce their meat intake, and do not drink wine or eat large meats; and place on the wound, should pus appear, use moist cotton in rose oil, or in astringent wine; and if there is no pus present, apply to the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood, and isn't disturbed by air, then powder that I will mention later; and if it has been disturbed, apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then join them through suture, as I will explain for wounds on the belly, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes bone, and can bleed but stays there for just a little bit if you press; then treat the wound with medicine, restore tough tissue instead of skin, and instruct the patient to consume large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat like bread, also things similar.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover rotten skin, and it doesn't reach the bone, then remove the rot completely, and let out pus, then treat the wound; and if there's an artery in the wound or vein, cut without hesitation, and cannot stop bleeding with medicines, so remove the artery, and if you find dislocation, tie it with a thread; and if this doesn't help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put on this powder which sticks together in such a way that when the heat of the fire has applied it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of applying the powder is as follows: take one part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; living charcoal three parts, and finely ground it all, then apply this mixture to the wound and press it firmly until it soaks well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it tightly, leaving it undisturbed if it doesn't swell; because you remove the medicine only when it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one does not do this using charcoal alone, when one lacks the incense or the blood of dragon, but only when the surgeon has cleansed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the stomach has healed the wound, indeed in that state, one must not apply this powder at all; but apply certain ointments or powders, such as flour of barley mixed with water and honey until it starts to drain; then continue other treatments until it is cured.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if bone bruising comes with the wound and it's small, pinch it gently; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	from the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound occurs in the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and those of the head, but if it affects the collarbone or the artery, then it is different.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, leave no cure and don't apply any restraining thing, as it harms the nerves and makes them recede; don't put anything cold on the wound because the substance of the nerves is cold and continues with the brain which is the highest member; but use medicine under that way, such as oil rinsed in gentle water and mixed with rose oil, and wet linen also in gentle water, and other earthy substances according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then treat it by binding with cloths.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, one should pierce them or lower; and if an artery is severed, bleeding follows - then one must open it, stitch it back together and cauterize. And if a nerve from the throat is cut, or blood vessels and tubes that lead to flesh must be kept in mind - through which meat goes. If a bone spur is cut near the throat hole, do not touch the throat but put it according to its natural shape; then keep it there for some days before treating with drying ointments until it heals properly. And if pressure has been made on the bone, take action accordingly; and if pieces of bone exist that you can remove, do so while those you cannot reach should be left alone until the wound heals and discharges properly; and if the wound is fresh, apply a powder as I've mentioned previously to it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones and an opening in the wound, treat it as described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, when you observe that wind blows around the wound without disturbing the patient: then you know the wound is fatal. If it's not deep and it's fresh with all its blood, don't apply any powder in the first hour, nor bind it due to the blood not draining completely from under, and returning into the heart, and making the patient dizzy; instead apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton into the wound for absorbing moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; so if there's no seizure, nor trembling in the heart, without any strain happening all alone; and when you see good results, knowing that the wound has been saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat then with various remedies until it becomes healed; and if it cannot heal or work, know that there is a fistula; proceed with the treatment as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it's simple or more severe or at the back, based on the treatment of the person before. If it's large, stitch it; and if it's small, use powder, and if it's infected inside the bone with fragments removed, if you treat the wound and remove the foreign objects; and if they are not removed, leave the wound to heal naturally, helping with extraction procedures; and for other wounds on other limbs, make judgments similarly as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	about the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The operations on the belly are large, medium, and small; for a big wound there might be no instance of an intestine tear or damage to its lining, through which foreign objects could enter. Stitching is more troublesome, and it's never worse than smaller wounds as when larger ones you have to repeatedly bring back the intestines in place until properly done; because if they feel cold and swell immediately afterwards, they do not fit back into their original places easily, thus making small wounds preferable. Knowing that the rupture of the belly can occur in four ways: The common two types of stitches happen during a stitch in the abdominal area, and the stitches for other body part injuries are usually shared with those other injuries; however, these still tend to be more efficient when compared to the abdominal injury repair operation, which I will explain further.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and no part of the intestine has been involved, and if there are things to be removed, this can be done by one of two methods: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or due to the fact that the intestine is swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat him in this manner: soak a sponge or dip a cloth into hot water just, or you may cook it in hot water with vinegar and pepper, and raise the intestine until the swelling disappears; and do this again after making that wine restorative to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or steam that has been well cooked, for through this the entry of small things is facilitated; and if it cannot enter, make a little incision in the wound using the tool used to remove stitches; and your first cure is to ensure smoothness rather than excessive cutting; unless there's great necessity, we should not cut more than necessary. And these are the tools for this purpose: you cut inside along the curve and outwards not too much, and thus you have this shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have escaped, if you can place it back according to its natural shape in its proper location, do so because this is better than having left them out.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is extensive, and it's in the abdominal region, it should be that you make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head. And if it's in the part below the abdomen, then position their head and buttocks above the lower parts; similarly, when there is an abdominal rupture in one of the two halves, adjust so that the removed part is higher than the other; and thus, you should follow my instructions for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use what is at hand, then take the necessary surgical instruments to clean out the entire wound, stitch it up and close it; this is a common method of suturing. Use needles or multiple needles according to the size of the wound. Leave two inches from the edge of the wound before starting your stitches, then place one needle with strong thread at that point. Insert the needles through both layers of skin at the points of each suture, and continue to pierce as far down into the flesh as needed. Then join the tips of the siphac (appendices) on either side three times together; sew them back tightly from two opposite directions using a double thread. Sew up any remaining edges of the wound in the same manner as you did with your first stitches, ensuring continuity throughout the entire process. The size and sharpness of needles matter; thinner ones cut through flesh, while thick ones may not fit well. Avoid placing needle holes too close to the flesh and skin edge which could widen the wound, causing pain when sleeping at night. Cover each needle hole with a piece of cloth or bandage for support, leaving them in place until the wound heals completely. This suturing technique works particularly well on small wounds; in such cases, one additional stitch might be required every second time you stitch together skin and appendices at a single needle point. After piercing all four sides three times each, pull out the needle from where you started, as if sewing cloth. Leave an inch between each stitch, which helps heal properly. This kind of healing enabled me to stitch a wound that someone had suffered with an open belly due to a knife cut; the wound was more than a palm in size and contained well two palms worth of intestines, and it was located in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine, then after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days. I treated it and it recovered, becoming healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when they had decided that he was going to die, it was a miracle; and I didn't treat him with ointment, because I was in the middle of nowhere where no such thing could be found, nor any medicine. Instead, I changed old cotton twice a day over the wound, washing it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie. de la voinne civile	from the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is present in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil lacking moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to corruption originating beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms do within the body, penetrating between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of this vein's beginning show, so that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then change its course, and the vein starts to emerge outward, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, it is necessary that you wrap around one third to three quarters of a piece of linen, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging on the leg. And every time there's a bit left over when cutting off, wrap inside the linen and tie it; and if it's too long, cut out a part, then wrap again, making sure not to cover its root until it's fully exposed. If you do cover it, it will enter the flesh, causing pus and decay or disease; thus this matter must be treated little by little up to the shoulder, leaving nothing in between; and only once the treated vein is five inches long, or ten, and roughly twenty paces from where it originated on me, does it become fit for use. Then you should cut off one inch or two ends of it, then pierce till you reach the bottom, so that everything comes out; drain any inner matter thoroughly, and prescribe medicine against putrefaction for a single day, then treat further as for pus.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And not once at this vein cuttings, and especially when it opens in the ankle or hip joint, where bones meet, causing much damage and where cuts are made. So then treat accordingly as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "cow disease," because it has often affected cows, and it's a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and it travels throughout the entire body, up and down, and its presence can be felt as it moves from one limb to another, until it reaches the skin where it was going, and it grows; and it becomes infected with pus from some fluids, like coming worms, snakes, and parasites such as roundworms or those of the stomach; and there is doubt about its malignancy, for when it travels through the body, and when it ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and bled, only then can one understand that as it proceeds: hence, it becomes necessary for you to bind the head above and below with a firm bandage tightly. Then cut upwards and drain it, and if there is no discharge in the flesh, if you fail to find any, then apply fire cautery on it until it starts bleeding; and the greatest harms that it causes, are when they go towards the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or beginning near the eye, then bind it firmly below him with a form, cut upwards, and drain; and one should use the aid of purification from body fluids by medicines that dissolve, and beware of eating cooked meats which cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from wind.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that affects any member, and spreads from one limb to another; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman and she showed me her arms. She had a small swelling in the veins near her elbows; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm was climbing up to her shoulder, faster than anything else, like hot silver cut from one thing to another; the pain left that part of her body and settled into her shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout her entire body until she reached her other arm. Then she told me that it twisted within her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how she moved member by member within my body, for I had never witnessed this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Always, I wanted to have many that well had wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it myself, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, with uncovered veins, and because of this constraint, this windiness appeared; and they do not appear like this when considering those who are delicate and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see treat this illness, and the patients feel this pain, if it opens as we have said, quickly above and below, then hold onto it for as long as that windiness escapes from its place; and cauterize your area; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat those who debout the windiness, such as stinking pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	Des saiettes" translates to "of arrows" in English. This term refers to objects that resemble arrows, likely referring to projectiles or weapons in historical contexts.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various depending on their shapes and according to where they pierce or hit the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of their shape consists in that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and that one chucks out nothing but in any member it chucks according to two manners: or in the principal members it sticks, such as head, heart, liver, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes to the shoulder joint specifically in these limbs, and the sign of death that I will tell you later on, they show: you should be prepared for extracting this arrow because death follows in various dispositions; and if this bad sign does not become apparent and the arrow is not fully extracted, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces through and lodges in the bone, and starts a fiery fluid near the brain, is followed by blindness, deafness, inversion of the eyes, redness in them, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and mental confusion, vomiting of pus; and sometimes loss of strength in the nose or ears; and perhaps loss of speech and voice; and a white moist exudate coming out from the wound that resembles pus, and also burns like charcoal; and if this sign appears, you should take action and remove the arrow if it's still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the dart when it bites or pierces, is that it's near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the dart also becomes silent like a pulse, with black blood and coldness coming out, and fever and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that one should not ignore is when foam does not come out from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns red, and they sigh loudly with a quivering cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow is found in the covering over the buttocks, it is located below the small ribs; and produces great pain and sighing; and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow is in the stomach by chance, then there would be nothing of undigested meat coming out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow is found in the belly or abdomen, and there's no passage of bile through the intestines, then there's no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow is stuck in the bladder, causing urine to spurt and escape, and patients feel intense pain: know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, including the arms and shoulders, neck, throat, collarbone, shoulder blades, spine of the back, ribs, chest, and legs, as well as seeming members, are safe according to several different positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the body's nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do that treatment.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow struck him in his armpit at the root of his nose: I probed it and pulled it out from another side through the fat of the ear; he was saved without serious harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And pulled out an arrow from a game that hit him in the fat of the eye near the eyelid, under the paper, and the arrow was stuck, not able to reach much beyond the shaft, and the arrow was big as a Turkish bow length without ears; the game player was saved, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And remove an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and that arrow had Arabic feathers on it: I let the skin go first, then made my way through with precision as I pulled it out, leaving the Christian sound.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the house, that was stuck in his belly or chest, and thought he was dying; then after thirty days had passed, if it didn't change its position; I cut into the arrow, attached something to it, and pulled it out without any bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you encounter a house with an arrow that has fallen or hit it on the back, and found the wound healed up inside; and stayed the arrow within, not changing its natural positions, nor did any harm come from its natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And there is another person who fell with an arrow in his face and had the wound stitched; and ever since has suffered great pain; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And one fell an arrow into the court of the princes' home, where it was stuck in his neck, being slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded. I was called for treatment after it was stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound quite narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it using all kinds of delicate methods, and didn't feel anything; and he was experiencing pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I placed an adhesive and digestive plaster on his neck because his ears didn't swell up; and then I saw the arrow's tip in his ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the plaster on the wound immediately, and treated it quickly, so that the patient suffered long, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and I told him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive aqua regia to the wound using my hands until it was opened, and I tested it; I felt the tip of the arrow moving towards my hand. Then I readjusted in the wound opening with that corrosive aqua regia up until I saw the head of the arrow visibly appear; then passed through very well for about four months, and then closed so much that I pincers worked on it from both sides and couldn't get out; then kept refining and engineering methods for tools, until I took it out one day with well-made pincers according to how its shape will be in the end of this chapter, while treating and leaving the wound open.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and after being sewn up, the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me about the quality of extracting arrows, so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot take everything into account; but wise masters compare well with very little knowledge, and regarding what is present and lacking, find a new work and a new tool, in removing foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows penetrate members or the point of entry according to two ways: either through the upper part where they enter, or from another side; and the one that enters through itself or where it is inserted, this arrow penetrates the flesh, and has done so no longer.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it stay until the bone is thoroughly cooked inside, and becomes soft; and then you'll see its release. Also, if it's stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like this for some days, and remove it each day; and soon it will jump. If it doesn't, pierce deeply inside all through the subtle forest, until the inner parts are fully widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and reaches to one of the organs near the brain, or any other event that I have mentioned opens up for the patient: do not remove it immediately but let it stay until it becomes level after a few days. Because if the arrow goes up to this point, it's a death sentence.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and not yet fully inserted to its depth, and stays without causing any harm for several days without a bad incident, then remove it with skillful extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is so deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply hot fomentations internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow has been returned into the body to such depth that it cannot be seen, and you want to extract it using all your strength; and if you sense it, then attempt extraction without any suitable tool; and if you can't due to the size of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, then make a cut as large as necessary; and try extracting the arrow if possible, and if there are ears attached to which it is held, remove the flesh that sticks out from both sides up until you can, then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow when doing this, so that it won't come out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, leave it until the shaft is completely rotten up to the elbow, then try again, for its extraction is easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if blood flow contradicts you during this process, apply what we have discussed in the treatment chapter; and protect against incision near nerves or veins. Position your arm as you might safely remove the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently. Place the patient according to their position just before the arrow fell, for that is the greatest assistance. If you can't, place them according to how the symptoms show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that came from the opposite side, or where there is no part of it present, or if the skin is swollen at the point we can't see or feel clearly: then cut upwards as far as your forceps can take hold, and then pull: should it jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand around as long as she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it can't come out, let it stay still for now, and then start extracting again until it comes out. And if there's part of the arrow left in there, pull that too till it's gone; and if it's just the head of the arrow remaining, and you're able to extract that way, use a tool with a pointed end so that the point of the arrow goes through the tool when you pull, making extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is within, you must remove all the flesh around or where it enters until possible, then clean the wound according to how it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is in or hits the chest or bladder or abdomen, and it's close, you must remove it; and if possible, cover it up. And avoid covering the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound, should stitching be needed; and treat until she heals.
