des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins from common causes
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which bleeding occurs are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen, namely: Two small ones that are behind the ears, called "grass" heads; and two arteries that are in two visible temples; and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, called "aspirers"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose; and two glands under the throat; and two veins above the lips from the mouth, these are the veins called "augerich"; and two veins along the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that we commonly treat are in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and is under the left costal area, and they call it the "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'large vein', and is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is either on the right or left side, and they call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and this is the one that we treat, which opens clearly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The salve-telle is the vein that's between the little finger and ring finger, and it can be found in two places; and in the leg and where the foot meets the shinbone are three veins: one is located under the bend of the shin bone on the left side, and the second larger one is at the ankle on the right side; and there's another vein called 'the knee', which is located at the ankle on the other side. In the other leg are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The healing of veins that are behind the ears is assisted by ancient cathar treatments and migraines; and the qualities of a healer as I tell you, and whether you touch your head with an inflamed area or on the veins where they are in a rough cloth; then pinch the inflamed area's neck to a pin, until both veins appear behind the ears under two heads: then hold them firmly with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, let it bleed; then take the lancet, and insert through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, cut out well the skin and vein both for two inches deep, and make blood flow until you see; then tighten and tie, until it is healed; and I have already told about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The healing of the two arteries located in the two temples, if it involves ancient embolization and thrombosis, along with water-induced tears; and the quality of this healer is as I say: it makes its neck tight until the two veins clearly appear open. It feels the pulse all over your thumb, then checks it further down. Then lift the hand above the vein at your index tip, and hold the scalpel there, lift the hand up again, and cut the vein, just like you did with other veins, and make a cut according to your need; then release the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it; and then bind them well, leave them until they heal. And we have spoken about their extraction and their operation, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The treatment of the sinew at the forehead is worth as much as the treatment of the cephalic artery in ancient diseases, and headaches, and heatstroke; and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the tool called 'drill', which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip at the vein, and press with your hand or another thing, allowing a little blood to flow according to how much you see; then free up the neck for the patient, and bind the vein until it is healthy and no part of the work has been done by a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it must not be that the flames are too much; and heal across because the bone is close, and by chance break the flames when they are delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The treatment of the two veins found in two sinuses, as well as heatstroke and overheating, and earache in the ear canal, and diseases affecting the face; and the quality of their treatment is that the patient twists his neck due to some tie when turning (as previously explained), then treat them, and make a cut somewhat long but slightly wider than the flame, because there is no flesh involved.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; then do a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The treatment of the neck when it's injured involves bleeding, and sudden release, as well as diseases in the face such as headache and redness that comes with fever, especially if the face is old; and the quality of the treatment lies in constraining the throat first, then pulling the nose towards your left hand, taking a thin flame long, and sticking it inside the lip at the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well completely. The fire will now begin to cure; and do not go too far with heat, apply bleeding gently according to your need, then stop it for one night as it recovers very quickly; this is how the flame works:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The treatment for the inner ears aids in tightening the ocelli, initiates mixing of fluids, helps with a multitude of diseases including ear infections and corrosion, as well as herpes. And the quality of this treatment lies in squeezing the throat on both sides just like we have said previously; and ensure that the doctor is present at the head of the patient, place the patient's head on the edge, then treat the vein for a bit longer than it is wide, applying bleeding carefully, or only as necessary. Then repeat elsewhere on another vein, after untangling this connection, squeeze the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave them until morning, ensuring that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	In the healing of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of veins in the mouth aids in closing wounds and helps with gum decay, lip cracks, nosebleeds and internal injuries.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of healing is to have the patient stand in front of you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left. You know them by the fact that they are black, and because inside them there are small, black veins: so take both of them, and if you don't recognize them, and you're in doubt, then take the bigger one from each part, and do the same for the two veins above and below these ones since it's the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	In the healing of injuries to the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are near the tongue helps after the head's healing and this is done through narrowing the throat, and treating eye diseases, and mouth illnesses; and the quality of a surgeon is to have the patient lying under sunlight with their tongue raised and look at each side for one black vein: then heal both of them, and don't overdo it since they are near the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut through which we commonly heal are healed according to two ways: or by placing them in contact with all iron hot broad, or with subtle olive oil such as knife blades, and they are called 'anisel'; and they are large and subtle according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mirthin flame is very well known, and it is quite wide as you can see:

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are in the throat, and in the neck, and in the stomach, and in the abdomen; and it's important for the healer to heal properly and be aware of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is hit, and bleeding follows, should it be necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said; and there must not be a grasping of the flame, but cutting it instead like before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein is not clearly visible, it may be necessary to extract it, and use another one; or you don't want any part of this, or you drain through the arm in place of this vein: it opens clearly; and you cut to the flame as before, just like we said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know how to locate the site of treatment, it should be done as follows: cut the arm so that you touch the site until you feel the pulse; then mark the site outwardly, and then tie the arm down, and cut towards the flame as before; and be careful not to puncture the artery when you see the site inflamed, because it is part of the artery: listen out for it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something protruding upwards as much as the urine of a child, and the veins are red and subtle, know that it is a vein: so then hurry up, place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger when the vein stops bleeding, an event that has happened many times; tie up the arm, and leave it like this, do not move the patient; proceed with caution and do not move until he is saved.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not cleaned, and you need it, and the medicine is not present, if you open the artery when it opens, because the head of the body retreats; and clean the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take the bark of a fir tree, and cut it, and take one half and tie it firmly up to the other side; if the wound stops bleeding, it is fine; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the bandages are not changed in multiple positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The treatment of the vein is aided in its middle section where it deals with blood from the head above and from the chest below, as it consists of the basilica and cephalic sections, as we have mentioned; and the physician must be careful about the nerve which is nearby, and if he doesn't go too deep and comes across the nerve, and inflames and injures the health, and by chance can't heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it doesn't open in any men for its subtlety, then you should let your hand guide the tool towards its end; and listen to the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment of the cephalic vein is beneficial, as it deals with blood from the head and assists in healing; and it is fitting for a surgeon to work on the olive flame or the mirtin flame, because it is the safest among all veins, since there is neither nearby nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Always aim for the lightest blow, and do not take offense if you must try it once, then attempt again; indeed in some cases the limbs swell after the first instance, yet there is no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about hygiene is that it's managed through force only to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and this hygiene should be done in one of the three veins: these are known as cephalic, faecal, and basilic; and you should clean yourself at the beginning of prayers on your knees, and during autumn and winter after meals, when signs of satiety appear; and you should wash on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Hygiene for illness prevention doesn't have a fixed time, but it should be done as needed each day or after meals at any hour; and it's not advisable to bathe children until they are fourteen years old or pregnant women only during the first quarter of their pregnancy up until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither should doctors treat the elderly who have surpassed sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one seeks to heal oneself, in whatever manner it may be, so that they must cleanse the intestines with a light cathartic if they have retained mucus, so that the veins do not draw out the excesses that harm the principal limbs; or cannot heal themselves if they are too full of meat, or drunk, as long as they lack strength, nor sputum-filled. And be wary when one attempts to heal after colic, and vomiting, and abdominal pain, and frequent urination, and labor, and staying awake, and indulgence in pleasures; then refine the humors, if it is too large due to food, drink or medicines; then bathe oneself, provided nothing prevents you from doing so for refining the blood, and healing of the wound from the third below the anus as we have said; and guard against this day of labor, pleasure and excesses, and do these things with joy. And keep the healer's hands above him higher than those who are healed, and rub his arm twice or three times, then loosen your tie moderately from the middle. For if it is too tight or loose, he cannot correct himself; and then rub your hands onto him until the veins swell and you can feel them. Then moisten the healer's palm with a little old oil, then place your right hand on that vein over his anus for a moment or two where one intends to heal, so that the blood does not clot and fail under the knife.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like strings when heated, and there are those that are full of windiness, so that when one puts them over the flame, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein. And thus it is with this type; and if the person heats the vein, then the wound becomes too narrow, for which reason the surgeons must be knowledgeable in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first try, that's good; but if not, it should be tried again slightly over where you were or quickly, depending on whether his arm is swollen.
