Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are being treated and are choleric, and if they feel too hot and inflamed; it should be that they consume cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and lettuce salads, and similar items; and eat small pieces, and pork chops, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with cold constitutions should drink honey syrup and moderately fragrant wine between old and new. They should eat small portions and pieces of small fowl like pigeons; on the day they're about to be suctioned, it's better for them to drink more than eat. It is advised to give some people neither triamcinolone nor muscat before or after suctioning, as this might strengthen their main body parts. Keep their stomachs light but ensure that those who are hot don't drink these substances.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed to cause irritation are those placed on the liver and in the lungs, and for gout, and on the belly and intestines and hips. Because this limb does not suffer from being pricked with wounds, and one performs it forcefully only to draw blood within the body. Like when we place them on the nipples when the child is breastfeeding; to remove the stickiness that exists in the body. Like we place suction cups on the belly and intestines to reduce the body's size; and removes pain, where there are swellings or stones exist, it removes by its attractive power accidentally the swelling, or empties out the stone from its place; and this is done when placed on the liver and lungs when there is retained stiffness. These suction cups are administered empty solely for suctions purposes. They are not administered together with fire under any circumstances, and they are filled occasionally with hot water, as in diseases with much weeping, and in such a manner one fills up the suction cup with hot boiling water, or with water that has cooked suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction tool used at fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two sticks of half a palm in length each by the circumference and in the middle one small notch as to pierce like an awl, so that it does not wound the patient when put on the limb; and in the middle there is a rod across from a spider or iron for inserting a candlestick, and they are made both large and small according to diseases and the size of those taking them; because children's suckers are different than those of adults, and thin ones compared to fatty ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus should we apply this suction cup to the limb: take the candle or thread and insert it through the rod which is within the suction cup, ensuring that light reaches the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, position your thumbs over the notch as we have said, so when you wish, if vapor escapes, remove the suction cup; and take the candle or thread in this manner, as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup then, which is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there should not be a ridge or an indentation, and it must only be used when it is full of water, and placed solely on the limb. And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without gloves they are only used in limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and when the limbs are clean of flesh, like elbows or knees, and others similarly; and the quality of their use is that whenever you find without gloves that are in sweet water without pollution, take them; then place a nut in sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing inside. And then bleed and suction them, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and place them on the without gloves; and when they are full, and start producing, if there is any part where you can place a suction cup, put it there because this yields very little afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not this way, raise the arm first from the easy position, and then from the difficult one very carefully, quite well indeed, then prick it. And if the skin becomes too raw after some time, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and place it on the wound until the skin is healed; and if the wound is multileveled, place ground vitriol or garlic and similar substances on it until the wounds are healed; or you put half of peeled beans in the arm, let them heat up to the arm level, they will now stop bleeding; and if there's need for more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not gather properly, rub on the bleeding area with fresh blood, or you stick a needle in it until the blood comes out, and then place something there; and as soon as they sense the blood, they will stop. And when you see that they are bleeding again, dust some aloes powder and finely ground myrrh or ashes on them, and they should heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine and the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that the foolish minds of these people delve into this chapter's content, something they would never see in any old books or read from letters; and because of this reason, this knowledge has been hidden in our land. I have not come across anyone with true understanding of it before, and I myself know nothing about it. My knowledge comes solely through the study of ancient books that I've extensively worked on, through experiments and by living a life accustomed to such studies; thus, I'm describing here what's contained within this chapter in its entirety, then simplifying it at the end, making everything very clear as to how the tools used are made and utilized, just like I did in those two chapters before this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it follows that we should outline the preface of this book, which covers the essence of speech and chapters where one's intelligence is engaged. We must remain truthful, so those who have experienced this know and learn this noble art, and also teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fractures, dislocations, twists or inflammation occur to any part of the body, you should quickly cleanse the patient from one side and the other, without allowing anything to disturb them; this applies especially for those who are weak due to old age, infants, or those with poor health. If their limbs are either too stiff or too cold (meaning they're not properly warmed up), or if they are being fed cold food, such as cold meats, bird meat and venison - you should also avoid alcohol and any fatty foods. Avoid filling them with too many foods that block the blood vessels in the body until you have doubts about an abscess developing or the spreading of material within a limb. If the patient starts to feel better after their initial treatment, continue treating them accordingly based on how they respond to your care.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones start to heal, it is necessary that one cooks the meat that causes excessive cooking or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and chestnuts, and peas, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this kind of cooking leads to more movement and heals the breakage faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that breaking bones in the elderly and weak cannot be properly restored or glued according to their nature due to the dryness of limbs, nor in those who are too tender, such as bones of small children; but do this, break into the bone you have broken and tighten the joints together again while you reinforce it just like before; don't finish your work abruptly and because of this, feed it with large meats as we said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	But the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all about fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is damage heading towards harvest, and another when sharpening, such as the cut of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if in damage with injury, and breakage with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner has its tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and it is known that the breaking of bone occurs when one's senses are twisted, opens well outward, and feels pressure from the hand; and when there is no twisting or sensitivity at the touch, and if there is no breakage; but it can well have twisting, or crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that went against its course, and are its two parts detached, you must now put them in equal points, as abscesses on either side; and if abscesses get infected, do not leave any day, until the abscesses heal. Then make it even at a movement that you can do lightly and wisely, and know that their restoration is easier than those with pieces; then tighten, as explained after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if bones have broken pieces, and are divided into two parts, whether it's in the hands or feet, or under your hand where it's a small limb, or at two tendons, or one tendon under your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken member parts have recovered, you gently reintroduce the additions to their places with movements as you can, and ensure there is no injury or pain from your actions; and adjust well both ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if you think it is not quite right: if the dressing is beautiful and do not strain too much; do not squeeze as those who bring about pus discharge and muscle contraction in their work, as we have desired many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in position, so restrain the patient that they do not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, nor on turning or any other manner. And ensure well that the limbs are securely set to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not properly in place, and you should arrange them in such a position that they do not feel any pain. And take care to set them straightly, so that there be no crookedness when they are restored; and the quality of the broken limb must follow what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, degree, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as wrists and ankles, etc.: it is proper to wrap them in soft and delicate linen; and for those that are larger, such as calves and thighs: it is proper to wrap them with a large and sturdy bandage, because wide bands embrace the entire big limb and restrict it evenly from all sides, so there is no twist. Then bind around loosely, three or four turns according to the limb, and hold your hand on the whole band slightly tight, then go above the breakage and tighten less, allowing the breakage a slight distance away; and soften the band slowly and gradually, until you touch quite a portion of healthy tissue, then start another band again, bind it around the broken part tightly; then go back to the area under the breakage and apply moderate pressure, neither too strong nor too weak. Just as we have said in the previous lesson; then place linen or bandage bands between the tightly bound areas until everything is evenly done, then fasten everything with a central bandage, and then properly place your pins if there's no pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing for abscesses above it, and which reduces the swelling, allowing it to remain that way for a few days; then press on your fingers, they should be of half the width of a reed securely pressed, or from a staff used in making pipes, or from palm leaves, and do so according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the fingers which one places on the break be slightly larger and wider than the others; and should be as long as fits for the size or grandness of the limb; then press them with your fingers in the same manner as you did at first pressing, then tie a small extension above it also like the first pressing; make them tighter later and less so now; and it must be that the thread is just right, not too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen; for if the thread is too thick, like those who make their pressings with linseed strings which are often twisted together, this leads to error, because the pressing will not be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit that there is less than two paces of space between each finger.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the pins after pressing them in their healthy places, put patches of linen or wool on them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is swollen and the joints are broken, I will tell you the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not fitting to restrain all broken limbs for the whole first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to apply these supports that after three or five days, or more depending on the nature of the abscess occurring; and here is the method of old plastering for restoring fracture, dislocation, and twisting: you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, use it, and this is the common way of using plaster to restore fractures in various positions, equally so for women and young children because it is not too strong or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take 3 barley grains and garlic and mint and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each in .x. 3 grams; and incense and aloes, each in .v. 3 grams; vinegar is also needed, .viiij. 8 grams; grind these into powder, then mix with plenty of egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, restoring broken bones quickly, and is suitable for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plastering method that is suitable for twisting: take mastic and white wax, each in about 10 doses; myrrh and aloes, each in nine doses; senna in six doses; Armenian balsam in ten doses, grind it well, mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for setting bones and joints, and relieving the pain that occurs, and sharpening uses bone, and bruising: take new wool, and cook it in oil and fat, and place it on them.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Bandages do not heal, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly applying the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for setting bones in case of bone fracture and to alleviate the removal of pus.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violet flowers, groundnut of each one; and grind, mix with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with wet coriander water, or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of reattachment more forcefully than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the healing of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismarrow, and flaxseed, balm, milkvetch, and saussage, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all take one part; and grind and mix with salt water, or sweetened water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that to restore strength in the fractured limb, one should apply a balm made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, more. He states it should be of neither too soft nor too hard texture.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should place on the broken limb to restore it, things dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of plastering that is useful for injury and pain: take mutton and feathers from cooked sheep or bird feathers, and mustard, and equal salt, and grind them together, and make a plaster with it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then let it set for a little while later, and be careful so the patient doesn't feel any pain or feels the bone moving in its place; if you don't let it set by hand for days. If pain starts at the limb, or itchiness persists without rest or swelling occurs, if this happens then hurry, remove it, apply the dressing immediately; take a light cloth and moistened sponge, dip them in water, and immerse the limb as long as the itching stops and pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, secure with a bandage until you're sure of healing properly; and manage the inflammation of the limb and relieve the pain, then start applying a fine dressing and a little more of the paste, but do not apply it as strongly as before; and be meticulous until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain, and swelling are present everywhere on the wound, and you need plastering and bandaging, then start again, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there is no change in the limb like what we have said before, and you only release it after three or four days, five, seven; and never leave it for more than twenty days according to observation until the healing process has begun, and approached union of flesh within. Then you should maintain stricter restraint than initially, allowing its body to swell as I've mentioned previously; if you see that the skin dries excessively beyond what's required, know there are no new wounds involved; then submerge it in hot water each time you release it, and do this every third day, and clean a little of the wound area. Through this process you will eliminate any remaining pus from the limb, and swiftly correct for the mistakes made by ignorant surgeons who force the limb back into shape: that is harmful, and such operations are dangerous; I see nothing else but patience and proper surgery as alternatives.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding the various methods of crushing.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and various shapes occur, with different causes being designated; for there are fractures made by the impact of a sword, and necks fracture all the bone up to syfac which is under the bone, just like in an axe or staff strike; thus this manner of breakage is called "axe-breaking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword penetrates through the bone from above to below, it is called this method of breaking "absolute"; and these are the large or small injuries from these two types of breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the stone, or through stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break close to the membrane beneath the bone or on the bone itself, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has healed within the bone as thin as hair, and the crack is small, thus it is called this type of breakage "hairline". And if the injury is made by hitting with stone or falling objects, or from something similar, causing the piece of bone to enter downwards and be stuck in between such like the candlemaker when they burn candles on them; if the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This occurs more often in those who have wet bones beneath, such as the bone of children; it happens in all these ways of breakage where small fragments are lost like stars; and I will speak about that in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaking through by removing them from above, and the inquiry into tests, and through corruption in the flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it in, if the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the breakage, be careful of adverse events due to the disease, and if you see no bad adverse event, such as vomiting bile, loss of appetite, expansion, fever, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, do not hesitate in diagnosis.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming mishap, yet you hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you and it is in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fifteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the pus around the bone becomes putrid, and the accidents that we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of bone comes up to where the membrane covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut through the broken section like this: and take hold of the root of the diseased head, uncovering on the bone in every way that you can, and around the appearance of the wound as much as you can. And if bleeding starts revealing the bone, or an abscess forms, use what is appropriate and then fill up the space with wet cloths soaked in rose oil; and allow the wound to rest until the abscesses are subdued, and are assured of stopping of the bleeding; then begin excavating through the bone according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut at a narrow slice in front, which is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And make another cut slightly larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you should have several different-sized cuts: some narrow and others wide, with each being sharp-pointed and made of iron; and when working on them lightly, ensure that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is too hard and doesn't penetrate, you must puncture it internally in such a way that you administer cuts with needles, not too deeply so they do not pierce beyond the bone's thickness, and there should be a margin of about one circle above the point, ensuring that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each goes to its place within the width of the bone, for you need needles for all sides; this is how three kinds of needle formations are:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing internally through the broken bone is to place one needle on the bone, and turn with your thumbs until you know that the bone has pierced. Then replace the needle a little further elsewhere, and do this all around, then cut in between the perforations of the bone which is located between the teeth, and do it more subtly than possible and gently as we have said, continuously until you pull out the bone to your hand or with no tool that you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it's necessary to scrape away what remains of the bone from all other tools like a file, but this one should be more robust and more delicate than another file; and if there is nothing left of small bones, or any scales, then gently scrape them with the other instruments; then heal the wound with preparations and treatments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of doing it is what Galien stated, which is more prudent; and he uses a lot of force, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should expose a part of the bone, at or near where the break appears to move, so that once you have exposed this part, you will place underneath the tip of this lens-shaped incision, with which we are dealing here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, and have the limb divided into two parts, so that you cut towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, such that you gently touch the entire bone, and take care to avoid the skin that lies beneath; if it is hard against the bone, then delicately strike it, for one strikes the bone without causing harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing through the membrane, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small fragments, then you should proceed after that roughness, and remove the scales using a fine razor. You must have different quantities of this tool to apply in each area most appropriately, according to the work and the appearance of the breakage.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are facing large razors, and then finer ones, and keep doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other delicate haircutting and breakage procedures, you should adjust your approach according to their orientation; this is something that cannot be adequately addressed by someone who has devoted themselves to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the boil is discovered, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound and soak it in oil roset, then place it on the wound. Then take another cloth doubled two or three times, soak it in wine and oil roset, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this more gently than possible so as not to weigh down the boil, then apply a bandage above this other cloth without applying too much force so that only the wound is treated. Leave it like this for one or two days until the abscesses are calmed, then remove the bandages and administer medications such as rosemary roots, tumeric flour, incense powder, and aristolochia, among similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, also administering gentle medications. And guard that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or allow pus to form, for when pus forms under the skin surface, it spreads and causes harm to the patient; as soon as something pungent is put on the boil, it becomes inflamed from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no accidents befall the patient, as we have said, where there is doubt, let it not cause fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no harm comes out except due to the medicine that we have placed on it, should such a virtue be present, then you must take one part of honey, and three parts of rosy oil and in wax one spoonful, and then put this mixture on your skin. After this, proceed with the customary treatment methods until it heals completely, as long as it is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are ever broken, or only one by itself, as these are two bones; and here below is cartilaginous tissue, which does not break, nor can it be bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you pinch your little finger or the back of your nose, and place this break inside your index finger, and out from the nostril, until the nose recovers its natural shape; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the area above the nose and cannot reach the nostril opening, it must be that you place him level with the tip of a knife slightly thicker than that.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then repeat this procedure, and try to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or the eighth day, when the abscess has been drained, then pinch at the base of your nose with a linen cloth piece, should the break be in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another one from the other side, if the break is on that side too; and let them be as thick as they fill in the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorative requires the application of butter to swellings, and one must change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I don't think it's correct, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a yolk butter, and with powder from grinding; then leave the swelling until the bone is hard and the cartilage has hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And instead of tents one uses goose feathers or no feathers at all, and if you have a half-cooked egg spread around them, and let the wound be open, and blow on the patient's lungs; or do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose in such a way that you are working on them, then place a wad of moistened cerotta or cotton in olive oil or in a drop of eardrop.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess breaks out, then cover it from outside with a plaster made of ground poppy seeds and incense powder mixed with yolk butter. Then place it on light bandages but do not bind them too tightly; and if the pieces break off easily with the nails, and they are broken into small bits, then use instruments suitable for this purpose to extract the abscess contents, treating each part while healing and bonding as necessary; and if there is no wound within the nails, and the treatment of the swelling, then place poppy stalks in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured from within, and there's no wound outwardly visible, only the breakage is outwardly visible. It doesn't split into two parts externally, rather it fractures internally; one can detect this by gently assessing it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary: if the breakage occurs in the right part, you should push your index finger into the mouth towards the side. And if the breakage is in the left mandible, you should use your right hand's index finger to push from outside and gently apply pressure on the inside of the breakage, then move it outward with the other hand evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is an internal fracture of the jaw in two parts, then it is necessary that you apply extension to both halves until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken mandible and put two strips of cloth above it; and place one large candlestick well made, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, above the cloth strip, and bind it as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, allow it to settle for three days, and then adjust what has become unfastened; apply plaster on top, mixing with powder from the mill with enough egg or flour of almond after removing the wax. And place wool lightly on top of the plaster. If the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, let it be until it heals; many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come out, apply what we have instructed repeatedly.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward nothing of the bone when it is removed; so skillful are the tools for extracting such substances that they suffice.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.

de la forcele	by the power

de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A fracture may occur in the shoulder joint or its middle section and not anywhere else due to an impact; if it matches the pattern of the fracture, then treat according to its natural form, using all possible methods. Then sprinkle with flour from a mill along with enough eggs and gentle wrapping, place double cloths over it; then place a large and subtle long stick slightly wider than the shoulder joint; ensure there are no movements anywhere in the shoulder region by placing woolen linings of the stick, making sure the stick is evenly placed. Then tightly restrict everything into one large band so that the stick does not move from its place, check each day; every time it loosens, tighten again, keep the stick even if it's too tight for the shoulder joint, have the patient lie on their side; and finally, after twenty or twenty-five days, the shoulder will be healed. And once this period is complete, release the restriction, you'll know it's healed properly as there's no bone that would easily settle in place.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The process of breaking the splint.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that are between the knife and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take one solid stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:

And tie two heads with two pieces of rope, and put them up top, securing the patient on one spot; then place the patient's broken arm on the stick until it reaches the elbow, maintaining a bend in the stick equal to half its length, then position this at any heavy object or where helpers can pull down; then set the broken arm so that the injury is level with both hands together, until the broken limb returns as it should.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus comes out, do not immediately tighten until after seven days, and apply grease-soaked wool in a gentle manner and with rose oil, until the pus coming out is relieved; then apply tightening, and how to apply this tightening is that you place the plaster over the wound, then join the arm under the shoulder support, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; apply the cloth, tighten it on the shoulder support, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its usual position, without anything preventing it, or if the bone isn't broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you suspect that the bone doesn't move, use braces, and place an extra large and strong brace over the wound, with one inch of space between each brace. Make sure that each brace is as wide as it can pass through the wound by three inches from each side; then apply tightening on these braces, just like I explained at the beginning of this chapter about wounds, more forcefully but without pulling away too much.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it concerns the arteries, as we have said.

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of nature breaks in a woman, if you make her stay enlarged, then incline her to the part of her back, and support her from behind; then fill the gap made by nature with cotton, and place it as large as needed; then stand up the woman and lift the back gradually, and then jump out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of nature, and bring the bone along with you; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinated, return her to this process, doing so for seven days or more: the break will be healed. If you see fit, take a bladder from a goat, tie it at the tip of a stick, and blow the bladder inside until nature takes back the break; then fill with cotton and leave it like that for some days, until everything is fine.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with wound
