And if the wound is healed, you should reapply vitriol, or if you don't have anything else, then restart the process of healing at the same time or on that day, or in case there are no pus discharges.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there are no pus discharges, let the healing continue up to the next day, until the pus is reduced. And don't touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you would be causing harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see bone broken out on the cheekbone exposed surface, it is necessary to place it gently with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not suitable to place evenly with your hands, you should use this iron tool that is made of metal, which has seven inches or six inches in length, and its width suits the size of the wound; for this, it's necessary for the molder to take three or four pieces, according to what they need for each treatment of broken bones; and make sure it's round but a bit thick so that it doesn't bend when you compress it on your limb during work, and be sharp in front and large at the middle forward part like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And called 'palanchon' because it is necessary that the crooked shoulder be placed on top of the bone tip. And it must be beaten once and only until it heals, making sure they are even against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold onto the tip of the bone until the instruments have the ability to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back as we said before, if you have an instrument suitable for this purpose or like a scalpel or a surgeon's knife at your power; then cut that which is stuck in the hard part of the bone and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and after the patient feels great pain, understand that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do as much as it fits in its place, then coat the wound with a black and clean liniment of wine; and if it's external; don't put any ointment or other thing that could cause oiliness on the wound, to prevent the development of decay and corruption; then give these treatments once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound exposed, cover the surrounding area entirely according to the size of the wound, and take great care not to restrict the wound with pressure; many times this mistake has been made, causing harm or corrosion in the patient; and make sure that the compresses are softer and less abrasive than other pressures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that possibly harmful incidents have occurred inside it, as we said earlier, and you find pain in your arm, then it does not suit to place plasters; but instead envelop around, in the place of plasters, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing and that the swelling has gone down, remove whatever treatment you have applied with vinegar, and apply a healing ointment, such as the fourfold medicine and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be positioned so that the bone comes into contact with a slight ease.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days continue and it can't heal properly at its place, be aware that there are small bone fragments causing this issue, so it is necessary for you to work on the wound with tension, and remove all these broken parts that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in the arm or any other form of decay, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he explains in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the body, as for example in the elbow or shoulder or other parts of large bones, if you do not treat it, because many die from this, but leave it until it heals; by chance, it will drain through it after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if possible; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns often come after the healing of the wound, especially when it's close to the joint. There is much to observe in the figure of the limb; and by chance, one cannot do the natural actions with the limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take caution therefore when it comes to these fresh burns: if you administer any of the restrictive medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sycamore bark, carob, and similar others, do so either individually or in combination with each other. Mix them with stoptive wine or enough egg or oil; then apply them in poultices on the affected area and hold them tightly but don't remove them daily. Remove it only when the nodules are gone. Or you can place it under a well-made piece of plaster because the property of plaster is such that it clears all swellings above limbs. If the nodulation turns into hardness like stone, requiring extraction, do so after applying a dressing until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which becomes weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: due to which it was bound too tight, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and could not reach the member's necessities; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excess movements, not in its time; or due to having little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment involves making the patient eat their medicine and make their body tender until the pus multiplies within them; then they provide baths and give them joy and rest. Then apply wax to the limb so that the wax attracts to the large pus, and rinse it frequently with warm water until the pus corresponds to the limb. And restore its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and if the bone was broken apart, then the form of the member becomes ugly. Nonetheless, it does not lose its natural function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break the whole limb anew; many people have done this in our land; these operations are criticized, and lead to great harms, even death. Still, if the fractures and injuries are fresh, then they should be soothed with hot water or medicines that soften tissues such as leaves of vismalve, roots, and mallow flowers and similar things. Then apply a moistening plaster made in this way; or take greased figs, grind them with corn meal, and other remedies that diminish the heat, and make a moistening plaster from these substances. Alternatively, you may use well-prepared yarrow, mix it with fat from geese liver or oil of sesame, and apply this as a plaster. Or take greasy figs, grind them with bran, and similar medicines to decrease the heat, and prepare a moistening plaster using these ingredients.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never does a node fuse by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And permit some movement to the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like bone, and requires being treated with metal tools, then up to the bone if it's necessary, you should make incisions delicately; and consider and apply study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens to none, if it fits now to bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	And if you delay, they swell the limbs, and by chance put them under pressure at their joints; it is not appropriate to move them at the hour when they are swollen: many times it brings pus and other pains. Nonetheless, whenever this happens, make a physician treat the patient, then let him alone until all the abscesses have subsided; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as the treatment comes to their joints.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downward, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are somewhat ossified at their locations, and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the feet, causing saliva from the mouth to spill out, unable to hold it, nor close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and done, you must quickly reset it without delay; and do it in such a way that the servants cut the head of the patient, and place one of their hands' pocket behind the joint of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation involves two parts; and the other hand should be extended outward to make them equal. And instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers should remain evenly placed, until they reattach in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they return to be sore, just as when the two jaws are together, should you use hot water and oil, so long as lightly moving them; do not overly force their movement back in place, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well with mellowing, one puts on wet cloths in a wad made from rosemary oil and beeswax; then binds it lightly with moist string. And the patient sleeps on their back, and their head is between two pillows, so as not to move neither to the right nor to the left, nor strain at all, but only consume light food until the pains cease and the jaws are healed. And then eat what they desire lightly, without working to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and restored.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be correctly placed within an hour and are not turning back to their original position, it leads to fevers and habitual swelling, and sometimes stomach upset, and occasionally vomiting of pure liquid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, it has caused death in eight days for the one who experienced it.
de la forcelle	from the forcible act or action
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot relieve from within the middle of the ribcage and down to the backside; it is dislocated only once outward, and one feels this well indeed.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies still on their back, and extends their arms; then presses them into your palm shape, and they will return. Then place it on the plaster, and bind it, and tighten it; and the shoulder which is opposite to the blade cannot dislocate; if not, and should it dislocate once, you must reset it to its proper place as we have said; then place it back onto the plaster and bandage, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed. And thus similarly is returned the shoulder of the spine when it has been relieved from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You should know that an shoulder dislocation occurs in three ways: The first way is when it dislocates towards the part of the scapula away from the pit; and the second way is at the part below the heel. And by chance dislocates above, this happens rarely; and doesn't dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for nerves; and multiple times dislocates downwards near the scapula, even to those with little flesh, because in these it happens swiftly; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps outwards and returns towards the pit.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men a blow or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess, and fears that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must experiment on it as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will recognize the dislocations when it moves towards the scapula, and there is differentiation between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find various manifestations between them; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and along the scapula to the elbow, as if it were an eye. And the patient cannot move their hand near their nose, nor make any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated above, it's not completely hidden, because you clearly find it at the elbow; and this way of dislocation cannot be cured until it's new, or when there's a baby involved.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the ministers to lift their hand from the malady above, then place their hands on the shoulder blade, and lift the joint up strongly towards its natural position; and the ministers lift their hand, extend it upwards, then put it beneath; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come as we have said after a few days, then the patient should be dipped in hot water; and apply soothing warmth and relief, such as decoction of rosemary and fenugreek and milk thistle in water, and apply this remedy; then bandage the patient's back, put wool next to his armpit, it shouldn't be too soft or too hard, then place your fingers on his heel under the wool, and lift up the shoulder joint with a strong upward movement, and pull your hand from under the ailment; and another assistant should cut the head of the ailment, so that it doesn't move downwards; this shoulder returns immediately now, and if you see that it is being reset in this manner: then make sure there's someone larger than the patient standing nearby facing his back, and push up his shoulder under the aid with one hand, lift the aid up so that the patient hangs down at an angle, and another assistant pulls your hand towards the belly from under the ailment.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the limbs are too light, he carries nothing weighing with him, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it, you can do it in another way too: and insert the long stick into the ground, so that the limb is like a piston, and neither too large nor too thick; then place it under the limb, but make sure there's something soft underneath, and let your limbs stay long on the stick. Then stretch out your hand from the other side in this formation, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it doesn't return through all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms wide and three feet long, which has a shape that allows its head to enter down the groove right inside the socket, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie the stick where the stick is covered with cloth underneath, so that the stick does not bruise the wound, then place it on the base under the wound; and extend your arm along the stick from its length, and tie the support on the stick, and the arm at the hand's head, then place the arm on one of a pitchfork's prongs of as wide width, and keep your hands down, and leave the body hanging from another side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is like this, in any manner, if you need to place an equal wool stick on the shoulder socket, then put the plaster covered with powdered mill grinding on top of this, along with incense and egg yolk butter spread all over the shoulder and around it. Then hold the addition from under the shoulder joint, tie the link onto the plaster, wrap your hands around its neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that he chew little at first, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then chew more after five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and not made soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the connection has been forced away by moisture or for another reason, then you must apply three cauteries to it, as was described in the previous chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not stay, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be placed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the buttocks, and breasts, or behind, if it is caused by pushing, stretching of hands, and administration in another place; and treat as long as it's clean.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes swelling in the limb, and prolonged movements, then use hot baths many times, until that swelling is relieved, and it returns to its first natural state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated by points and comes back by points; it has been dislocated from all sides, even in front and behind; such a dislocation cannot be fully restored because one can clearly see and feel its extent; and it's dislocated according to every figure.

Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is necessary to reset it this way that the abscess is opened and heals, for if it were left closed after incision, it would be painful to try and reposition; and by chance it cannot be fully returned in all ways, even when it's behind; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And this restoration is as follows: when you can bring it back to its position, extend his/her hand with both of your hands; and the arms should be spread out, and the hands guided towards the elbow from front to back, backwards and forwards, and push the joint towards its socket or at the base of the palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there's a dislocation in front, it returns when they double their hand onto the other hand, and push with the blade at the base of the palm where the dislocation occurs.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it doesn't return to its place, you must apply strong extension; and when you do this, extend the arm with both hands, then rub it with both hands, so that it does not move during extension. Then bend the arm in every direction, having wrapped a double length of cloth around it from top to bottom; and when you are trying to join the joint back together with your hand, apply oil to help soften the joint, then force the joint into place until it begins to heal; and once it is in place, cover it with dry plaster mixed with egg yolk, then gently bind it again, keeping the arm at the neck level of the shoulder, and leave it for a few days, then remove the binding.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then release the ligament and leave it as is; and if you see that the joint is not properly fixed, reapply the plaster and the ligament, leaving it like this for a few more days until it's firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if they feel sore after setting the joint back in place and it moves again, bathe them well and rub vigorously, pressing until they are relieved. Or you can put a layer of fatty sheep's wool on the joint, leaving it for one day and one night, then apply the ointment, and allow them to bathe; and when they sweat, gently rub the joint, then replace the wool, and let them bathe again; and do this two or three times until they are healed. If possible, place a moist calf's stomach, heated with butter, on top of the joint; if it returns to its rightful position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Doing the realignment of the ankle and back.

des dislocations de la hainche	Regarding hip dislocations,
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier. And the signs of him who comes to face it, so these events are well with his leg according to its completion; nonetheless, he does not double bend the knee without pain, and if you try to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he passes on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes. Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption. Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be extended immediately with the affected leg, as I have said; and place his face towards his pain being on the side of the affected arm, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards to the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if a dislocation is in the back, it does not require extending the patient backwards or lifting them up from the ground. Instead, they should stay as they were when their hip was dislocated backwards, as we have explained about lying on both hips; and stay on their stomach, and extend the limbs like we said previously, and must press against the joint at the table; it is right when the patient extends their legs, and they are level. Then adjust the thighs, apply the plaster, tighten with one band so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then dislocate again, and apply plaster over it; and if you see they are level, apply pressure, as before, and let them rest for three more days; then dislocate again, and have them walk properly until the limb is reinforced.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Regarding shoulder dislocation due to joint displacement,
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can be dislocated in three ways: to understand this, it is within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the symptoms are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee. If they cannot touch their knee, know that it is dislocated; and for the restoration of all this, make the patient stand upright, extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their buttocks, then put their foot on yours. Then take their knee with your palms, pull it between your fingers, then bend both sides from under the knee firmly; and another helper should extend their foot as long as the knee returns to its place, and you will know that they lightly bent well their leg at the knee; and apply the plaster, have the leg burn against the knee, and keep them together tightly for three or four days, then release; do not disturb the patient's walking until their limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if there's no motion of limbs at all, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is restored.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never fully set and always partially dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if there are such signs that the ankle is swollen and tends to move towards the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning should be gentle, and one must gently extend its hands when it feels slightly back only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you should have the patient sit upright and guide them with their legs out from under the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and twice more to the left, then lift it up straight, firmly hold the foot up high; and perform this twice as we said, while lifting and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's well; if not, continue with the procedure because it will return; and if it can't return this way, make them lie down on their back on the ground, plant one leg firmly in the earth between their buttocks, bind bandages around them so they don't bruise the ankle; then shave the buttocks and have another guide lift the foot to their hands or to a line, which they tie around the neck of the foot; then extend each guide evenly, and place the bundle firmly under the buttocks for the ankle's support when you stretch it up; then hold the eyes level with the dislocation at their hands, and have another guide shave the healthy leg above the knee, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at its point, put the plaster and bandage above, compress firmly, bind with the foot, and watch that no nerves under the ankle are pinched. Make sure not to tie too tightly; then let it be for two or three days, and if it comes loose in binding, remove it. Then release on the third day or fourth, and give rest to the patient for four days; and should he surpass this termination, it is not certain that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses are put on and they come out, it is necessary that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are sound.

Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, if they can be beautifully extended through laborious effort, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no part of the back or foot, it should be made to rest on his full length or flat on a table completely straightened out, and put your foot where it opens at these joints, then press with your foot firmly until he revives; and when he is equalized, and there's nothing opening, place under the sole of his foot a table with two shoulders, then compress firmly, and let him rest for three days, then release. And make him to rest until he is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding injuries and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in your treatment, if you are inexperienced with the art or have not used it for a long time, and if you lack pity and mercy, don't be rash; and at the start use things that soothe and help in abscess drainage, and leave the patient to God's care, if you do not see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, immediately reset the limb back into place, as with the draining of pus; and when the limb is back in place, give soothing and antiseptic treatments for abscesses, and treat the injury properly, using dried ointments; and if due to dislocation there's breakage and small bone fragments, you should set them, and follow what we've said about simple diseases; and beware of entering a path of fear according to what I've said, because this comes from your Creator and through knowledge for the care of yourself and your body.
